  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f63056be-50bc-477a-b679-9e74d54c45d2'

Remi’s life includes a number of surprising twists and turns, leading to a clim</span>
  <span id="freeText5838645895391938933" style="display:none">A compelling story in which orphaned Remi gets hired out to a traveling street entertainer when his foster parents fall on hard times. Remi’s life includes a number of surprising twists and turns, leading to a climax and a very happy conclusion when he is reunited with his family.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5811476338789192791">Sans Famille = Nobody's Boy = Alone in the World, Hector Malot<br/><br/>Sans Famille is an 1878 French novel by Hector Malot. The novel was reportedly inspired by the Italian street musicians of the 19th century, in particular the harpists from Viggiano, Basilicata.<br/><br/>Jerome Barberin lives with his wife in a little French town, Chavanon (on the edge of the Central Massif, near the origins of the river Loire).   <span id="freeText5811476338789192791" style="display:none">Sans Famille = Nobody's Boy = Alone in the World, Hector Malot<br /><br />Sans Famille is an 1878 French novel by Hector Malot. The novel was reportedly inspired by the Italian street musicians of the 19th century, in particular the harpists from Viggiano, Basilicata.<br /><br />Jerome Barberin lives with his wife in a little French town, Chavanon (on the edge of the Central Massif, near the origins of the river Loire). He usually works in Paris as a mason. One day he finds a baby boy in Paris. The boy wears very fine clothes, so apparently his parents are rich. Barberin offers to take care of the child, hoping to get a good reward. He gives the boy to his wife, and calls him Remi.<br /><br />Barberin gets injured in an accident. He blames his employer and hopes to receive financial compensation in a trial. The trial costs a lot of money, and Barberin tells his wife to sell her cow (her main source of wealth) and to get rid of Remi. She does the former.<br /><br />The story proper starts when Remi is eight years old. Barberin comes home unexpectedly, bitter and penniless, having lost his trial. He sees that Remi is still there and decides to get rid of him when he meets a travelling artist, Signor Vitalis, in the local pub, who travels with three dogs - Capi, Zerbino and Dolce - and a monkey, Joli-Cœur. Vitalis offers to take Remi on as an apprentice for money.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و پنجم ماه دسامبر سال 2004 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: بی خانمان؛ نویسنده: هکتور هانری مالو؛ مترجم: روحی ارباب؛ تهران، گلشائی، چاپ دوم 1335، در 238 ص؛ چاپ ششم 1364، در 360 ص؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان فرانسوی - سده 19 م<br /><br />عنوان: بی خانمان؛ نویسنده: هکتور هانری مالو؛ مترجم: افسون مهدویان؛ تهران، ویژه نشر، 1382، در دو جلد، چاپ دوم 1394، در 560 ص؛ شابک 9789647440554؛<br /><br />عنوان: بی خانمان؛ نویسنده: هکتور هانری مالو؛ مترجم: حبیب یوسف زاده؛ تهران، افق، 1393، در 541 ص؛ شابک: 9789643698645؛<br /><br />این اثر به صورت خلاصه با ترجمه فریدون معمار در انتشارات شهرزاد در سال 1372 هجری خورشیدی، حسین صوفی در سال 1343 هجری خورشیدی، محمدتقی دانیا در انتشارات توسن، در سال 1362 هجری خورشیدی، جمشید بهرامیان در سال 1385 هجری خورشیدی نیز به چاپ رسیده است<br /><br />داستان بی‌ خانمان؛ روایت زندگی پسری به نام رمی ست، که در زمان تولد ربوده می‌شود. پس از رخدادهایی گوناگون آقای باربرین و همسرش، او را به فرزندی می‌پذیرند، اما به دلیل تنگدستی، رمی را به یک نوازنده ی دوره گرد می‌فروشند؛ و ...؛ ماجراهای هیجان‌ انگیز این پسر مهربان و شجاع، داستان خودباوری و مبارزه با سختی‌هاست. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_480429425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/480429425" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/480429425?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      501 Must Read Books (Children)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=501">501</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer480429425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3448916714231422145">This is a coming of age story of <b>Remi Barbarin</b> a 6-y/o Italian boy who is adopted by a poor couple when they find him abandoned in front of government building where Mr. Barbarin works. However, Mr. Barbarin's motive of adopting him is with the hope that someday the infant baby in silk clothes (hint that the baby's parents are rich), will be asked back by his parents in exchange of a huge money. Years passed and when Mr. Barbarin feels that it will no longer happen, he sells the boy to a perform</span>
  <span id="freeText3448916714231422145" style="display:none">This is a coming of age story of <b>Remi Barbarin</b> a 6-y/o Italian boy who is adopted by a poor couple when they find him abandoned in front of government building where Mr. Barbarin works. However, Mr. Barbarin's motive of adopting him is with the hope that someday the infant baby in silk clothes (hint that the baby's parents are rich), will be asked back by his parents in exchange of a huge money. Years passed and when Mr. Barbarin feels that it will no longer happen, he sells the boy to a performing artist, <b>Vitalis.</b><br /><br />Vitalis owns a roadshow troupe that goes all around Europe to entertain farm folks. With him are three trained dogs and a monkey called <b>Jolie-Coeur.</b> Tragedy strikes and Vitalis dies. Remi, now a young man, is left to fend for himself and his animal friends. He decides to look for his real parents and so half of the book is about that quest. I will not tell you further what happens because it will be too much of a spoiler. The ending is happy so this is still an appropriate Christmas read. Hope, indeed, is eternal.<br /><br />What I liked about this book was the very simple and innocent voice of the narrator-child. When Remi narrates, his voice oozes with sincerity so you can't help but have your heart really go for him. It reminds me of the boy Frank McCourt in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/252577.Angela_s_Ashes" title="Angela's Ashes by Frank McCourt" rel="nofollow noopener">Angela's Ashes</a> (4 stars). It's just that this book, <i>Nobody's Boy</i> was first published in 1916 (first English translation) so this obviously came first.<br /><br />Another noteworthy aspect of the story is that Vitalis treats Remi as a son. This is a clear departure from the usual story of this kind where the one who buys the child (with the purpose of having the child to work for him) from the foster parent(s) is so devious that the poor child becomes a force to reckon with in terms of eliciting water from your tear ducts. In the story, the bond that gets developed between Vitalis and Remi is so pure and strong that it can even compete to the usual father-son relationship that we see around.<br /><br />Lastly, the book gives us a glimpse of the life of performing roadshow artists during the late 19th century countryside Italy, Paris and other parts of Europe. How I wish there were more vivid descriptions of the locales that could have made this book more memorable. I love looking at pictures of the old Paris. Lovelier than now, I think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3448916714231422145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_513870823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513870823" />
    <a title="Christopher Bunn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4636657-christopher-bunn"><img alt="Christopher Bunn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348432236p2/4636657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513870823?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher Bunn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher Bunn" href="/user/show/4636657-christopher-bunn">Christopher Bunn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513870823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14176093316245355883">Hector Malot wrote Nobody's Boy back in the 1870s. It's a very slow, dreamy story, completely lacking in the speed and cliff-hanging and spectacle that define modern writing. I suppose a lot of readers would find his story boring or somewhat maudlin, but I found myself entranced by the combination of word precision and a sensation of something akin to gliding slowly down a river. A river in the French countryside, of course, apropos to the story, gleaming with lazy summer sunlight.<br/><br/>Malot's use of</span>
  <span id="freeText14176093316245355883" style="display:none">Hector Malot wrote Nobody's Boy back in the 1870s. It's a very slow, dreamy story, completely lacking in the speed and cliff-hanging and spectacle that define modern writing. I suppose a lot of readers would find his story boring or somewhat maudlin, but I found myself entranced by the combination of word precision and a sensation of something akin to gliding slowly down a river. A river in the French countryside, of course, apropos to the story, gleaming with lazy summer sunlight.<br /><br />Malot's use of words is something worth noting. He's not necessarily a standout in this regard. I imagine most writers from that era were equally as careful and as precise. However, reading Nobody's Boy again hammered home to me how focused writing is from older times. Malot uses words the way they are supposed to be. There's no ambiguity in choice and application. The right word in the right place. There's no sloppiness. He knows his definitions and connotations. (Obviously, I read a translation from the original French, so I'm making an assumption here that the translator was just as careful and as faithful in his English version as Malot was with the French.)<br /><br />That kind of craft is so radically different from the general, run-of-the-mill writer these days (self included, I'm afraid). Most modern writers toss words around like tossing oatmeal against the wall. We use words imprecisely, not always grasping connotation and meaning correctly. This results in messy communication, shoddy motivations and awkward dialogue. Our bad writing is complicit in the overall decay of language.<br /><br />I found Nobody's Boy a refreshing draught in terms of language, in addition to the dreamily enchanting comfort of the story itself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14176093316245355883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I was a little creeped out at first because the book kicked off with Rémi being BOUGHT and taken away from his foster parents by a strange old man. Gosh, this probably looked different to a XIX century reader! But it turned out to be a nice children's book with traveling, animals, a caring father-figure etc. <br /><br />I really liked Sans Famille and the characters.</span>

I read it for the first time years ago when I was in elementary school(I’m now 22) and ever since I've re-read it quite a few times… I totally recommend it to EVERYONE, not because it’s MY fav book, but because the story is wonderful, it never stops being up to date and it ALWAYS manages to make you feel the same things… I can go read it right now, and I will STILL experience the same sadness, happiness, anger, surprise, hearbreak… I will STILL burst into tears</span>
  <span id="freeText980147151680021216" style="display:none">This is actually my favorite book. I read it for the first time years ago when I was in elementary school(I’m now 22) and ever since I've re-read it quite a few times… I totally recommend it to EVERYONE, not because it’s MY fav book, but because the story is wonderful, it never stops being up to date and it ALWAYS manages to make you feel the same things… I can go read it right now, and I will STILL experience the same sadness, happiness, anger, surprise, hearbreak… I will STILL burst into tears at specific points, as if I'm reading it for the 1st time… It’s magical how Malot does that… And, keep in mind, the original is written in French and I read the translation(I don’t know French unfortunately…), which is not even in English as Greek is my native language… I’ve heard somewhere that translation “takes away” about 70% of the original story, which for this book, I can’t even grasp!… Anyway… I should probably say sth about the plot…<br /> <br />We meet Remi in this book, a boy who is born without knowing where he came from or who his parents or family are in a small village in France. It’s safe and spoiler free to mention that Remi ends up with and old man after being sold to him (!!) and from then on we see how his life rolls on with the good and the bad and the difficulties… The title “Sans FAMILLE” has a point as the main issue is family; how it would be if he had a family; how it is now that he doesn’t; how that affects him… It’s shocking how the life being described is this of such a young child! It’s hearbreaking… But in the end -which is what I love about the book- you understand the title perfectly. I’m not sure if saying what it means will be a spoiler so I won’t, but it makes you realize that family is very important; however, not necessarily the family you were born with…<br /> <br />As said, I read the translation, so I’m not sure how and IF I can judge the writing, but from what I read I liked how the book flows and how the suspense is built, how you love every page of it… It contains EVERYTHING; literally, EVERYTHING! Everything there is in life… I don’t see how someone could not love this book… And what’s more fanscinating is that the book was written in 1878!! Can you believe that??<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="980147151680021216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16084722702508616222">This book, though not originally written as a children's classic, has been considered one. This is only one of the traits it shares with Dickens' Oliver Twist. Both novels chronicle the tragic wanderings of foundlings whose only desire is to belong somewhere. In both cases, the boys are pursued by those who wish them ill and in both cases, they are nearly sucked into a life of crime. Remi, though as unlucky as Oliver, receives more kindness and assistance, generally speaking, than his English co</span>
  <span id="freeText16084722702508616222" style="display:none">This book, though not originally written as a children's classic, has been considered one. This is only one of the traits it shares with Dickens' Oliver Twist. Both novels chronicle the tragic wanderings of foundlings whose only desire is to belong somewhere. In both cases, the boys are pursued by those who wish them ill and in both cases, they are nearly sucked into a life of crime. Remi, though as unlucky as Oliver, receives more kindness and assistance, generally speaking, than his English counterpart. He travels more, observes more and learns more. He also has more control over his own fate, but makes some stupid mistakes, because after all, the drama cannot end too quickly, nor should the resolution of his problems be too easy. <br /><br />This picaresque novel is melodramatic in many places, but also contains much beauty, much humour, and many memorable characters, both human and animal. Who can forget Vitalis the itinerant actor, Capi the canine savant, or Joli-Coeur the temperamental yet loveable performing monkey?<br /><br />[I should not write reviews late at night. So many typos! It's a good thing we can go back and edit!]</span>
  <a data-text-id="16084722702508616222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8840198944968710366">I first saw this as a cartoon when I was 8 years old.. it broke my heart.<br/><br/>I read it 15 years later.. It broke it all over again.<br/>I had to stop at several points to take a breather and dry my eyes.<br/>Even as I write this review I find it difficult to keep my tears at pay.<br/><br/>Remi is a sweet little child who'll capture your heart from his very first moment..   <span id="freeText8840198944968710366" style="display:none">I first saw this as a cartoon when I was 8 years old.. it broke my heart.<br /><br />I read it 15 years later.. It broke it all over again.<br />I had to stop at several points to take a breather and dry my eyes.<br />Even as I write this review I find it difficult to keep my tears at pay.<br /><br />Remi is a sweet little child who'll capture your heart from his very first moment.. From the very first line I was hooked *I knew I would be since I dearly loved the cartoon, but to read is it, it's a whole another experience*..<br /><b>I was a foundling. But until I was eight years of age I thought I had a mother like other children, for when I cried a woman held me tightly in her arms and rocked me gently until my tears stopped falling. I never got into bed without her coming to kiss me, and when the December winds blew the icy snow against the window panes, she would take my feet between her hands and warm them, while she sang to me.</b> well, what is a mother if not that? Mother Barberin though may not appear a lot in this book but she her spirit shines through.. she's the force that keeps Remi going and when he starts earning some meager money.. first thing he thinks of is to buy her a gift ='(<br /><br />Everyone in this book is befelled with one tragedy or another.. Everyone has another story going on for them..<br /><br />I don't think there's a chapter I haven't cried on.. not only the sad events or the tragedies are what bring tears to my eyes.. no, it's also the goodness and warmness that touch my heart.<br /><br />If you're not ready for your heart to crack.. don't read this.. but if you endured it.. have no worries.. your heart will heal just perfectly because <b>no matter how heart breaking this may be, it has the most perfect of happy endings</b>.<br /><br />I regret not reading this in it's original language *French* but perhaps someday, if I managed to resurrect and nourish my knowledge of it, I might just do that.. I know I'll fall in love with it even more &lt;3.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13015144344889958568">Another gift, this one from my sister, which I enjoyed very much (still only gets 3 stars for being heavy-handed). It's a reprint of a classic 19th-century French novel (in English translation; the original title is "Sans Famille"), about the adventures of a boy separated from his family. <br/>According to Project Gutenberg, it is "justly famous as one of the supreme juvenile stories of the world." Apparently it has been translated into about a bazillion languages and made into films in a number of l</span>
  <span id="freeText13015144344889958568" style="display:none">Another gift, this one from my sister, which I enjoyed very much (still only gets 3 stars for being heavy-handed). It's a reprint of a classic 19th-century French novel (in English translation; the original title is "Sans Famille"), about the adventures of a boy separated from his family. <br />According to Project Gutenberg, it is "justly famous as one of the supreme juvenile stories of the world." Apparently it has been translated into about a bazillion languages and made into films in a number of languages, too. Next up: "Nobody's Girl," which my sister remembers as one of her favorites from when she was a child. I thought I would start with the boy's story, since it was written first, and no doubt it's popularity led to the author writing a similar book about a girl.</span>

  <span id="freeText7776492098648783861" style="display:none">3.5+<br />mid 1850s<br />mostly in France, a few chapters are set in England<br />rec: a map of France<br /><br /><i>I am a foundling.<br />But until I was eight years old I thought I had a mother, just as all other children did.</i><br /><br />So begins the story. Remi is indentured to Vitalis who walked the roads, stopping in towns and cities to perform with three talented dogs, a monkey, and a metal fife. After making his 'deal,' he had a young boy to add to his troupe.<br /><br /> What follows is a series of adventures, both bad and good, all of which shape young Remi's character.<br /><br />Some explicit advice on p 65: <br />• <i> Always be attentive and patient, my lad. Whatever you have to do, do it the best you can. Don't ever forget that.</i><br />• <i> You gain little by being brutal. You gain much more, if not quite everything, by being kind.</i><br />Vitalis goes on to explain that fear paralyzes the mind and a person who has fits of temper will come across as untrustworthy.<br />These sentences aren't typical; most of the lessons are 'taught' by example, not by words.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Everything turns out splendidly for Remi, with all the loose ends coming together smoothly. Probably the most over-the-top- fairytale ending that I've ever read. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It think <u>Adventures of Perrine</u> is a better story ... but it's been 5 years since I read it, so I can't say that with much confidence.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325924595" class="readable"

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14622456362391763896">I loved this story, and I highly recommend it. It's a story about a boy that finds out he's adopted, and is set on a journey to find out who he is.<br/>It' s a great book, well written and brings all types of emotions threw out the whole story, it makes you laugh, it makes you cry, it makes you angry and disappointed, but like all good books, it ends with a happy ending, and it deserves it.<br/>It shows a different setting of what me (like other teenagers) look for, it's set in a time we don't live in and</span>
  <span id="freeText14622456362391763896" style="display:none">I loved this story, and I highly recommend it. It's a story about a boy that finds out he's adopted, and is set on a journey to find out who he is.<br />It' s a great book, well written and brings all types of emotions threw out the whole story, it makes you laugh, it makes you cry, it makes you angry and disappointed, but like all good books, it ends with a happy ending, and it deserves it.<br />It shows a different setting of what me (like other teenagers) look for, it's set in a time we don't live in and sometimes it's hard to understand, but anyway, it's good to change sometimes.<br />Even when I found this book great, I'm a little disappointed with the ending, like I already said it ends good, but I feel that Hector Malot rushed it a bit, it wasn't written with so much details as the rest of the book, and from where Remi starts looking for Mrs Milligan it was rushed and was fast, it passed from one idea to another really fast and made you get lost a bit.<br />Even with this small point, I enjoyed the book and if like reading story's set in other times, that bring all kinds of emotions (especially sadness and pity, even when their funny a happy parts) this is a book for you, it's written in a simple language and isn't hard to understand, and it's good for relaxing and having a good time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14622456362391763896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Igm1fruSYEC+AvuMUpefZ8IlifpuhhbS9jZFDtNel697Qb8BYhzZxJGz4FQGEFzBHHmTmOEijxA33Hos12574w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kmh3ggO4dWJTbSXrXLIE8PfeyIbJEc82okriqV4gBKbLIH392jbM5nzcPjMINcdWKYLS5Ea1VvRjoN2LWhDo6g==')})
  }

            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1516687.Hector_Malot">About Hector Malot</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1516687.Hector_Malot"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1285258030p3/1516687.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7482881929044123030">Hector Malot was a French writer born in La Bouille, Seine-Maritime. He studied law in Rouen and Paris, but eventually literature became his passion. He worked as a dramatic critic for Lloyd Francais and as a literary critic for L'Opinion Nationale.<br/>His first book, published in 1859, was <i>Les Amants</i>. In total Malot wrote over 70 books. By far his most famous book is <i>Sans Famille</i> (<i>Nobody's Boy</i>, 1878)</span>
  <span id="freeText7482881929044123030" style="display:none">Hector Malot was a French writer born in La Bouille, Seine-Maritime. He studied law in Rouen and Paris, but eventually literature became his passion. He worked as a dramatic critic for Lloyd Francais and as a literary critic for L'Opinion Nationale.<br />His first book, published in 1859, was <i>Les Amants</i>. In total Malot wrote over 70 books. By far his most famous book is <i>Sans Famille</i> (<i>Nobody's Boy</i>, 1878), which deals with the travels of the young orphan Remi, who is sold to the streetmusician Vitalis at age 10. <i>Sans Famille</i> gained fame as a children's book, though it was not originally intended as such.<br />He announced his retirement as an author of fiction in 1895, but in 1896 he returned with the novel <i>L'amour Dominateur</i> as well as the account of his literary life <i>Le Roman de mes Romans</i> (<i>The Novel of my Novels</i>).</span>
  <a data-text-id="7482881929044123030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
